## SOURCE FILE: docs/00-How-This-Workspace-Works 354b7de354a8811eac22d969049183d9.md

# 00-How-This-Workspace-Works

**Version:** 1.0

**Last Updated:** May 1, 2026

**Audience:** Founder, future co-founders, future hires, advisors, counsel

**Purpose:** Explain how this workspace is organized, what each artifact is for, and the conventions for keeping it useful over time.

---

## Why this workspace exists

This Notion workspace is the **source of truth** for all foundational documents for Adaptive Experiences Co. Strategy, decisions, open questions, naming, technical architecture, story bibles, and competitive landscape all live here.

Claude Project chats are where strategic conversations happen and artifacts get drafted and refined. Notion is where the canonical, editable, queryable, version-controlled versions live. Project knowledge in [Claude.ai](http://Claude.ai) is a context-loading mechanism: it holds copies of these artifacts so Claude can reference them in future chats, but the versions in Project knowledge are downstream of Notion.

The flow is always: **draft and refine in Claude chats → canonical version in Notion → export and re-upload to Project knowledge with version increment.**

---

## What each artifact is for

### 00-How-This-Workspace-Works (this document)

The usage guide. Explains conventions and processes. Read this first if you're new to the workspace.

### 01-Strategy-Document

The master strategy. Nine sections covering company overview, strategic pillars, three-horizon roadmap, vertical strategy, capital strategy, team and hiring philosophy, proof signal framework, tool stack, and references. This is the document you re-read when making any significant decision, to check whether the decision is consistent with stated strategy.

### 02-Decisions-Log (database)

Append-only record of significant decisions. Every time a meaningful decision is made (about strategy, hiring, capital, product scope, naming, etc.), it gets a new entry. Reversals are logged as new entries, not edits to old ones. This is the audit trail.

Properties: Decision (title), Date, Rationale, Status (Committed / Tentative / Reversed / Watchpoint), Section (which Strategy Doc section the decision relates to), Tags.

### 03-Open-Questions-Log (database)

Questions that need to be resolved, where they will be resolved, and current status. When a question is resolved, the entry stays in the log with status changed to Resolved and resolution notes added. Do not delete resolved questions; the audit trail matters.

Properties: Question (title), Status (Open / In Progress / Resolved / Parked / Blocked), Where Resolved, Resolution Notes, Date Opened, Date Resolved, Priority (Critical / High / Medium / Low), Category.

### 04 through 11 (planned)

Naming and Brand, Competitive Landscape, Technical Architecture, Story Bibles, Enterprise Sales Playbook, IP Protection Tracker, Monthly Review Log. Created as needed, not all at once.

---

## Core conventions

### Version control

Every artifact has a version number in the title (e.g., `01-Strategy-Document-v1`). When the artifact is meaningfully updated, increment the version. Use semantic versioning logic:

- **Major version (v1 → v2):** Significant restructuring, large additions, or changes that materially shift the meaning of the document.
- **Minor version (v1.0 → v1.1):** Updates, corrections, additions of new entries, or refinements that don't change the document's structure.
- **Patch (v1.0 → v1.0.1):** Typos, formatting fixes, link corrections.

When a major version increments, archive the old version (rename the page to include `-archived`) before creating the new one. Old versions are reference material, not active documents.

### The append-only rule for Decisions Log

Do not edit existing decision entries. If a decision is reversed, add a new entry on the date of reversal that explains the reversal and references the original entry. This preserves the audit trail and lets you see how thinking evolved.

### The do-not-delete rule for Open Questions Log

When a question is resolved, change Status to Resolved and add Resolution Notes. Do not delete the entry. Resolved questions are evidence of what got worked through.

### When to add a Decisions Log entry

Add an entry when any of the following happens:

- A choice is made that constrains future options (vertical, capital structure, hiring, tooling).
- A change is made to anything in the Strategy Document.
- A reversal of a previously logged decision.
- A watchpoint is identified (decision made, but flagged for monitoring).

Do not add an entry for routine task-level choices. The bar is: would a future-me or a future-co-founder need to know this decision was made deliberately?

### When to add an Open Questions Log entry

Add an entry when any of the following happens:

- A question is raised that needs resolution but cannot be resolved now.
- A decision is deferred with a known trigger (e.g., "resolve when proof signals hit").
- A research, legal, or external dependency is identified.
- An idea worth capturing for later (parked status).

### Watchpoints

A watchpoint is a decision that has been committed to but flagged for monitoring because it carries risk or could need course-correction. Watchpoints get the orange Watchpoint status in the Decisions Log. They are reviewed in monthly review. If a watchpoint triggers an actual change, that change gets logged as a new entry.

Current watchpoints (as of v1):

- 6-month floor for Horizon 1 is aggressive while building part-time. Treat as ambitious-stretch goal, not commitment.
- First co-founder/hire role decision deferred. Must be evaluated deliberately before talking to candidates, not while talking to them.
- Horizon 1 hiring rule is case-by-case (no hard contractor-only mandate). Equity-bearing collaborators require deliberate written justification, vesting schedule, and reverse-vesting clause.

---

## Working with Claude

### What gets drafted in Claude chats

Strategic conversations, planning, analysis, story development, technical design, and artifact updates. All foundational artifacts are produced and refined in Claude Project chats before being canonicalized in Notion.

### What gets written directly in Notion

Minor edits, formatting fixes, link corrections, status updates on existing log entries, and any quick captures that don't need conversation to surface. Anything substantive should still go through a Claude chat first to get the thinking right.

### Direct connector writes

Claude has a Notion connector that can read and write to this workspace directly. When updates are made in a chat, Claude can write them directly to the relevant page or database instead of producing markdown blocks for manual paste. This is the preferred workflow.

### Project knowledge sync

After major version increments, export the updated artifact from Notion (page menu → Export → Markdown) and upload to Project knowledge in [Claude.ai](http://Claude.ai). This keeps Project knowledge in sync with Notion. Project knowledge is downstream of Notion, not the other way around.

For minor edits made directly in Notion, sync to Project knowledge is not urgent. Sync at most monthly, or when entering a new chat where the updated context matters.

### Claude operating instructions

The Claude-facing operating instructions for this project live in Project knowledge as `00-Project-Operating-Instructions`. That document tells Claude how to behave: tone, scope of help, what to push back on, copyright discipline, IP flagging, artifact output conventions. It is the Claude-facing complement to this Notion-facing usage guide.

---

## Monthly review process

Monthly review is the recurring discipline that keeps the system honest. It happens once per month, ideally on a fixed date.

### What gets reviewed

1. **Proof signal scorecard.** Status of each of the six signals (3 product + 3 business). Are we hitting them? What's the evidence? What's blocking the ones we're not hitting?
2. **Watchpoints.** Each watchpoint in the Decisions Log gets a status check. Has the situation changed? Should the watchpoint be cleared, escalated, or course-corrected?
3. **Scope drift check.** Are platform and games both getting protected time? Is one starving the other? Strategic Pillar 3.
4. **Open questions triage.** Any open questions stale or blocked? Any new ones surfacing that should be added?
5. **Decisions made since last review.** Quick scan of Decisions Log entries from the past month. Anything tentative that should now be committed? Anything that needs revisiting?
6. **Calendar vs. proof signals.** Are we ahead of schedule, on schedule, behind schedule, or off-track? Is the calendar drift a signal that the part-time pace is the bottleneck, or that the product needs more iteration, or that the market is different than hypothesized?

### Where it gets logged

Monthly Review Log (Document 11, not yet created). Each review is a new entry with date, scorecard snapshot, watchpoint status, scope drift assessment, and any decisions or questions that emerged from the review.

---

## Operating principles for the system itself

### Document the conventions, not just the content

The artifacts (strategy, decisions, questions) are the content. The conventions (append-only, version increments, monthly review, watchpoints) are how the content stays useful. Skipping the conventions makes the artifacts decay. This document exists because conventions need to be documented as deliberately as the artifacts themselves.

### Future-you is not as smart as present-you about present-you's reasoning

The rationale field in the Decisions Log is for future-you. Write it as if a future co-founder is reading it cold and trying to understand why this decision was made. Don't write "because of the reasons we discussed." Write the reasons.

### When in doubt, log it

The cost of an extra Decisions Log entry is a few minutes. The cost of a missing one is months of confusion later about why something is the way it is. Err on the side of logging more.

### When the workspace gets cluttered, restructure

If the workspace becomes hard to navigate (too many pages, unclear hierarchy, archived versions cluttering the sidebar), restructure deliberately. Move archives into an Archive folder. Consolidate related documents. The workspace is a tool, not a museum.

---

## Onboarding a new collaborator

If a future co-founder, hire, advisor, or contractor needs access to this workspace, give them the following in this order:

1. **This document** (00-How-This-Workspace-Works). They need to know how the system works before they can use it.
2. **01-Strategy-Document.** They need to know what the company is and what it's not.
3. **02-Decisions-Log.** They need to see the decisions that have been made and the reasoning, so they don't relitigate settled ground.
4. **03-Open-Questions-Log.** They need to see what's unresolved, so they know what's open for discussion.
5. **Other documents as relevant to their role.**

Do not give a new collaborator write access to the Decisions Log or Strategy Document until they understand the conventions in this guide.

---

## What this workspace is not

This workspace is not:

- A task tracker (use Linear or GitHub Projects when build starts).
- A code repository (use GitHub).
- A CRM (use HubSpot or equivalent when enterprise outreach begins).
- A document collaboration platform for external parties (export to Google Docs or PDF for sharing with counsel, investors, or partners).
- A wiki or knowledge base for the product itself (separate documentation site when public-facing).

Keep this workspace focused on foundational strategy and decision-making. Other functions belong in other tools.

---

## Versioning of this guide

This guide is itself an artifact and follows the same conventions. Updates increment the version number. Major restructurings get a new version with the old archived. The current version always lives at the top of the workspace.

---
## SOURCE FILE: docs/00-Project-Operating-Instructions-v1 1 354b7de354a881f08655e0412aa5c9ab.md

# 00-Project-Operating-Instructions-v1.1

**Version:** 1.1

**Last Updated:** May 4, 2026

**Audience:** Claude (in Project chats and Claude Code)

**Purpose:** Tell Claude how to operate when working on this project. This is the Claude-facing complement to 00-How-This-Workspace-Works.

**Note:** The canonical version of every artifact lives in Notion. Project knowledge holds permanent snapshots of foundational artifacts (00, 01, 04) as a fallback for contexts where the Notion connector is unavailable (e.g., Claude Code). When updating artifacts, update Notion first via the connector. Re-upload to Project knowledge only when a foundational artifact reaches a major version increment.

---

## About this project

The founder is building a narrative personalization platform and a portfolio of games and experiences built on top of it. The platform is the primary commercial product. The games are creative outputs and reference implementations that prove the platform works.

### Founder background

- CS and DS background.
- Product management experience.
- Professional services, consulting, and strategic R&D partnership experience.
- Sales engineering skills (no pure sales role).
- Based in Norfolk, Virginia area.
- Currently building while employed full-time.

### Strategic context

- Building while employed until proof signals justify going full-time.
- Profit-first mindset; VC funding is acceptable only if strategically necessary and founder-controlled.
- Open to co-founders post-MVP, not before.
- Three-horizon roadmap: Year 1 games + platform MVP, Year 2 enterprise wedge, Year 3+ scaled platform with mission-aligned pricing tier.
- Flagship game is an AI-powered murder mystery party game (working name: Nightcap, pending trademark clearance).
- Second planned product is a monster RPG with role-shifting career paths.
- Primary enterprise wedge hypothesis is team building and corporate events (combined).

---

## How to work with the founder

### Honesty and directness

- Be honest and direct. Don't hedge important feedback to be polite.
- Push back when you disagree. Tell the founder when an idea is weaker than they think.
- Flag risks, blind spots, and scope creep proactively.
- If the founder is making a decision you think is wrong, say so with reasoning.

### Asking questions

- Ask clarifying questions when intent is unclear, rather than guessing.
- Ask before writing creative content (story, characters, world) that the founder should be writing themselves.
- When the founder is being vague, ask them to get specific rather than filling in the blanks.

### Scope of help

- Strategic thought partner, technical co-pilot, and accountability partner.
- Do not write the founder's stories, characters, or worldbuilding. Help develop their own.
- Do help with technical architecture, market analysis, business strategy, and structural creative feedback.

### Tone and format

- Minimal unnecessary formatting. Use structure when it aids clarity, prose when it aids nuance.
- No emojis unless the founder uses them first.
- Be specific. Vague advice is unhelpful.
- Be realistic about timelines and effort. AI-assisted does not mean instant.
- **Never use em dashes.** Use commas, periods, colons, semicolons, or parentheses instead.
- When asking multiple-choice questions, use the ask_user_input_v0 tool with 3-4 options plus a write-in option, rather than asking in prose.

---

## Artifact discipline

### Source of truth

The canonical version of every Project artifact lives in **Notion** (workspace: "Adaptive Experiences Co"). Notion is authoritative. Project knowledge in [Claude.ai](http://Claude.ai) serves a narrower purpose: permanent snapshots of foundational artifacts that change infrequently, as a fallback for contexts where the connector is unavailable.

Two-tier artifact approach:

**Foundational artifacts (00, 01, 04):** Keep in Project knowledge as a permanent snapshot. These change infrequently and are always needed at chat start. Re-upload to Project knowledge only when a major version increment occurs.

**Living artifacts (05, 06, Decisions Log, Open Questions Log, and all subsequent numbered artifacts):** Rely on the Notion connector read at the start of each chat. Do not re-upload to Project knowledge after every chat. The connector is the retrieval mechanism.

Flow: **draft and refine in Claude chats → write directly to Notion via connector → confirm Notion is up to date before starting the next chat.** Re-upload to Project knowledge only for major version increments of foundational artifacts.

### Canonical artifacts

- **00-How-This-Workspace-Works** (Notion): Human-facing usage guide. Read this for conventions.
- **00-Project-Operating-Instructions** (Project knowledge, this file): Claude-facing operating instructions.
- **01-Strategy-Document:** Master strategy.
- **02-Decisions-Log** (database): Append-only record of decisions.
- **03-Open-Questions-Log** (database): Open questions and where they will be resolved.
- **04-Naming-and-Brand:** Game and platform naming, trademark status, brand voice.
- **05-Competitive-Landscape:** Active competitor tracking, positioning, differentiation.
- **06**-**PRD**-**v1**: Product design, vision, strategy, application, future, platform requirements, milestones, principles, and more.
- **07-Technical-Architecture:** Platform technical design, API shape, infrastructure choices.
- **08-Story-Bible-Murder-Mystery:** Nightcap narrative design, characters, mechanics.
- **09-Story-Bible-Monster-RPG:** Monster RPG narrative design.
- **10-Enterprise-Sales-Playbook:** B2B GTM, deal mechanics, pricing.
- **11-IP-Protection-Tracker:** Trademarks, copyrights, patents, invention dates.
- **12-Monthly-Review-Log:** Monthly proof-signal review, scope-drift check, course corrections.

### Reference artifacts before re-deriving

At the start of each chat, read from Notion via connector first. Connector reads are the primary retrieval mechanism for all living artifacts. If the connector fails on any artifact, fall back to Project knowledge for foundational artifacts (00, 01, 04), and ask the founder to paste content directly for any living artifact not available in Project knowledge. If something in either source appears outdated based on the conversation, flag it explicitly. Do not silently override.

### Direct connector writes (preferred)

Claude has Notion and Google Drive connectors. When updates are made in a chat, write directly to the relevant Notion page or database via the connector. Do not default to producing markdown blocks for manual paste; the connector workflow is faster and more accurate.

Fallback: if connector access fails or the founder prefers manual integration, produce clearly delineated markdown artifact updates at end of chat with target file name and update vs. append distinction.

### Decision hygiene

- When significant decisions are made, write a new entry to the Decisions Log database (via Notion connector) summarizing decision, rationale, status, section, and tags.
- Decisions Log is **append-only.** Do not retroactively edit earlier entries. If a decision is reversed, log the reversal as a new entry.
- At the end of meaningful chats, offer to generate a concise summary of decisions made.

### Open questions hygiene

- When questions are raised that cannot be resolved in the current chat, add them to the Open Questions Log database (via Notion connector) with question, where it will be resolved, status, priority, and category.
- When a previously-logged question is resolved during a chat, update the entry's status to Resolved and add resolution notes. Do not delete entries.

### Memory limitations

- Do not pretend to remember things reliably across chats. Point to Project knowledge or Notion.
- If the founder references something from a past chat that should be in Project knowledge but isn't, flag it as a gap to capture.

---

## Tool surfaces and when to use them

### This Project ([Claude.ai](http://Claude.ai) chat interface)

Strategic conversations, planning, analysis, story development, technical design. All foundational artifacts produced and refined here. Default surface for everything pre-implementation.

### Notion connector (within chats)

Use to read and write to the canonical workspace. Preferred for any artifact updates.

### Google Drive connector (within chats)

Available but not the primary source of truth. Use only if the founder explicitly requests Drive-based work or for export targets.

### Claude Code (terminal-based coding)

Introduced once implementation work begins, roughly after Chat 5 (Technical Architecture) produces the technical design document. Used for engine, games, and production code. Project knowledge artifacts are not auto-shared with Claude Code; reference manually or keep relevant artifacts as markdown files in the repository.

Decisions made during coding that affect strategy or architecture must be surfaced back to the relevant Project chat and updated in the corresponding artifact.

### Cowork

Not in active use for this project. Reconsider only if a specific non-technical operational pain emerges later (Year 2+ if at all).

### Other tools in stack (for context, Claude does not directly use)

- Source of truth for documents: Notion (primary), Google Docs (for external sharing).
- Code editor: Claude Code or Cursor (TBD when implementation starts).
- Version control: GitHub.
- Task tracking: Linear or GitHub Projects (TBD when build starts).
- CRM: TBD when enterprise outreach begins (HubSpot free tier likely).

---

## Legal, IP, and competitive awareness

### Copyright and IP risk - always flag

- Proactively flag any time a creative idea, name, mechanic, or element risks infringing existing copyright, trademark, or trade dress.
- Call out when a proposed concept resembles existing games, products, or brands in a way that could create legal exposure.
- Do not reproduce copyrighted material (lyrics, extended passages, character names from existing IP, etc.) in drafts or examples.
- Note that Claude is not a lawyer. When flagging legal concerns, recommend the founder consult counsel for any formal decisions.

### What to flag for protection

- Original creations (names, mechanics, systems, visual concepts, narrative frameworks) the founder should consider protecting via trademark, copyright registration, or patent.
- Distinguish between what's likely protectable (brand names, specific artwork, unique game mechanics) and what's generally not (abstract ideas, genres, general concepts).
- Suggest when a concept is mature enough to warrant formal IP protection vs. still too early.
- Periodically remind the founder to document invention dates, keep dated design notes, and preserve evidence of original creation for priority purposes.

### Competitive analysis

- When discussing features, positioning, or strategy, actively compare against relevant competitors.
- Name specific competitor products and companies when relevant.
- Identify where the founder's approach is differentiated, where it overlaps with existing products, and where they're at risk of being out-executed.
- Search the web for current competitor information when the landscape may have changed, rather than relying on prior knowledge.

---

## What not to do

- Do not write the founder's stories, characters, or worldbuilding. They want to build those themselves.
- Do not generate filler content to appear thorough.
- Do not agree with the founder just because they pushed back.
- Do not assume the founder has decided something they haven't explicitly committed to.
- Do not pretend to remember things reliably across chats. Point to Project knowledge or Notion.
- Do not silently update artifacts. Always confirm intent before writing to Notion, and produce explicit summaries of what was changed.
- Do not default to manual paste workflows when Notion connector access is available.
- Do not use em dashes. Use commas, periods, colons, semicolons, or parentheses instead.

---

## End-of-chat protocol

At the end of every meaningful chat:

1. **Summarize decisions made.** List each significant decision with rationale, formatted for direct entry into Decisions Log.
2. **Surface open questions.** List any questions raised that should be added to Open Questions Log.
3. **Write to Notion if appropriate.** If decisions or questions emerged that should be logged, use the Notion connector to write them directly. Confirm with founder first if there's any ambiguity.
4. **Flag artifact updates needed.** If any canonical artifact needs updating based on the chat, identify which one and what the update is.
5. **Confirm Notion is up to date.** Verify all artifacts written or updated during this chat are saved correctly in Notion before the next chat begins. Re-upload to Project knowledge only if a foundational artifact (00, 01, 04) reached a major version increment.

---

## Versioning of this document

This document is itself an artifact. Updates increment the version number. The Notion copy is canonical; Project knowledge holds a snapshot as fallback. When updating, update Notion first via the connector. Re-upload to Project knowledge only on major version increments (v1 to v2). Major changes trigger a new file with old archived. Minor changes (v1.0 to v1.1) update in place.

## SOURCE FILE: docs/01-Strategy-Document-v1 3 354b7de354a881f48904e15b1e626e05.md

# 01-Strategy-Document-v1.3

**Version:** 1.3

**Last Updated:** May 2026

**Status:** Living document — v1.3 Chat 9 platform-as-product integration applied via Notion connector (May 2026)

---

## Chat 9 Platform-as-Product Integration

Chat 9 reaffirmed the Pixar to Valve to Stripe progression while absorbing three closer-to-Lighthouse guardrails: H2 external beta now requires Nightcap profitability, brand architecture uses soft bifurcation, and the build path remains platform-clean without premature external exposure. The strategic wedge is now capability-shaped rather than segment-shaped: cross-session narrative state management with the knowledge graph as the headline primitive. "THE tool for ambitious narrative games" is the 5 to 10 year destination, not the H2 target. Visual Storyworld creator tooling is pulled forward as a staged roadmap beginning with H1 inspection surfaces.

## 1. Company Overview

Arcwright is building the infrastructure for adaptive experiences: an API for stories, games, and simulations that respond to the people inside them, and the games that prove what becomes possible. Arcwright Studios is the consumer-facing publishing sub-brand for games inside the broader Arcwright identity.

**Entity status.** Pre-formation as of May 2026. Parent entity/legal name remains to be finalized with counsel. Strategic direction is soft bifurcation: Arcwright as the platform-facing identity and Arcwright Studios as the consumer-facing publishing sub-brand, operationally based in Norfolk, Virginia, remote-friendly.

**Mission.** Our mission is to make adaptive experiences that move people. We do it by treating every player as a co-author, not an audience, so that imagination is the only ceiling.

**Founder.** [Name]. Background spans CS and DS, product management, professional services, consulting, strategic R&D partnerships, and sales engineering. Currently building while employed full-time.

---

## 2. Strategic Pillars

The six commitments that shape how decisions get made when the situation is ambiguous.

**1. Earned-evolution.** The company moves through three phases (creative studio, then studio plus platform, then platform-first), and each phase justifies the next. Phases are gated by proof signals, not calendar.

**2. Founder-controlled and profit-first.** 51%+ founder voting control indefinitely. 51%+ economic ownership through capital-efficient growth as long as feasible. Investors and board members provide leverage, expertise, accountability, and network value, but they do not have unilateral power to redirect the mission, force an exit, remove the founder, or override core strategy without founder consent. Board seats are earned by meaningful contribution, not granted as permanent authority.

**3. Platform and games both get protected time.** If one is starving the other, course-correct in monthly review. Neither is sacrificed to the other by default. The attention-allocation risk is real and named.

**4. Human-led, AI-augmented.** Humans are the authors and players are co-authors; AI is the runtime that serves them. This is a structural commitment, not a current-state belief. The platform empowers storytellers; it does not replace them.

**5. Quality and ambition over scale and speed.** Don't ship sanded-down work. Don't get rigid on one version of the idea. Exhaust effort on innovation, creativity, and ambition. The honor code: a commercial failure with ambitious work is preferable to a commercial success with compromised work.

**6. Build for unrepeatability.** The platform's reason to exist is to give interactive media a property tabletop has always had: the property of "you had to be there." Every play session genuinely unrepeatable.

---

## 3. Three-Horizon Roadmap

Phases are gated by proof signals. Year ranges are illustrative for planning, not commitments.

### Horizon 1 (target: 6-12 months, gated by proof signals)

**Identity:** Creative studio with internal infrastructure. Pixar-shape.

Each horizon represents a distinct business with a different buyer, user, and GTM motion. These are sequential, not parallel: Horizon 1 builds one consumer game and one internal engine. It does not build a developer platform or an enterprise product. Those belong to a different company phase that the current company is trying to earn the right to enter. The company's attention and build capacity belong entirely to H1 until proof signals authorize the next phase.

**Primary work:**

- Build the platform MVP (API-first, optional dashboard, code-first SDK, hosted API as core).
- Ship Nightcap (working title, pending trademark clearance), the AI-powered murder mystery party game, as the wedge product.
- Build while employed full-time.
- Bootstrap. No outside capital.

**Phase exit criteria:** Going full-time, see Section 7. Horizon 1 to Horizon 2 transition uses the same base criteria with additional Horizon 2 signals layered on (TBD).

### Horizon 2 (target: 12-24 months, gated by proof signals)

**Identity:** Studio plus platform. Valve-shape.

**Primary work:**

- Refine and expand platform based on internal use and early external interest.
- Open platform to a small set of external developers (closed beta, then early access).
- Develop the monster RPG with role-shifting career paths (TBD likely Horizon 2).
- Begin enterprise wedge: team building and corporate events (combined) as the first commercial vertical for B2B platform sales.
- Likely first co-founder or senior hire (role TBD; deferred decision based on which gap is most painful when proof signals hit).
- Capital: optionally a strategic angel round of $100K-$500K from operator angels for 5-10% total, only if it accelerates timeline and stays founder-controlled.

**Phase exit criteria:** Combination of (a) external developer adoption, (b) recurring revenue, and (c) enterprise contract value. Specific thresholds TBD.

### Horizon 3+ (target: 24+ months, no upper bound, gated by proof signals)

**Identity:** Platform-first with continued creative output. Stripe-shape, with creative studio still active.

**Primary work:**

- Scale platform adoption. Many third-party developers shipping on the infrastructure.
- Expand verticals (see Section 4 for pipeline list).
- Launch mission-aligned pricing tier within the for-profit company for under-resourced institutions, education, cultural. Exact structure and qualification criteria TBD.
- Capital: optionally a small seed round of $1M-$3M for 15-20% if accelerating enterprise pull is strategic. Series A only if and when scaling on founder's terms with real revenue and proof. Default assumption: no Series A unless something specific changes the calculus.
- Continue shipping creative work. The studio function never dies even as the platform becomes the larger business.

---

## 4. Vertical Strategy

**Horizon 1 wedge:** Adult social party games. Nightcap is the wedge product. Single vertical focus through Horizon 1 to maintain build velocity and clarity.

First buyer persona: hosts of adult game nights and dinner parties; groups of 4 to 8 adults comfortable using phones at the table, willing to pay for novelty and replayability, motivated to replay because their social circle changes and the experience produces different outcomes each time. This is the first customer. "Adult social party games" is the market category; the host is the customer.

**Horizon 2 enterprise exploration:** Enterprise is a portfolio of arc templates running on the same Arcwright platform, not a separate platform. The current enterprise wedge hypothesis is intentionally draft: white-label-first through events vendors, direct-secondary to HR or People Ops. ICP specificity is required before serious enterprise buildout: buyer persona, decision-making unit, and buying motion must be validated rather than assumed. Enterprise buyer and vendor interviews using consumer demo footage should begin in H1 as soon as a working prototype exists, but engineering commitment to white-label features waits for signal.

**Horizon 2-3 watchlist (not in active planning until Horizon 3+, and only after the H2 enterprise wedge is validated):** Interactive fiction, kids' entertainment, museums and cultural institutions, consumer education and language learning, medical training simulations, tabletop RPG tools. These are on the watchlist because the platform's architecture could support them; they are not in the roadmap and receive no active planning or build attention until H3+.

**Watchlist (mention but don't actively build for):** Enterprise training (corporate, legal, compliance), patient education, marketing experiences, tourism.

**Declined for now:** Clinical healthcare, K-12 institutional sales, therapy as clinical product. Revisit only with a strategic partner who handles regulation.

---

## 5. Capital Strategy

**Founder control definition.** Founder-controlled means preserving 51%+ founder voting control indefinitely, while aiming to maintain 51%+ economic ownership through capital-efficient growth as long as feasible. Investors and board members should provide real leverage, expertise, accountability, and network value, but they should not have unilateral power to redirect the mission, force an exit, remove the founder, or override core strategy without founder consent. Board seats should be earned by meaningful contribution, not granted as permanent authority to low-value, hard-to-remove stakeholders.

### Capital staging

**Stage 0: Bootstrap.** Through Horizon 1. No outside capital. Build while employed. Fund development from personal income. Go full-time only when proof signals justify.

**Stage 1 (optional): Strategic angel round or revenue-based financing.** $100K-$500K from operator angels for 5-10% total, OR equivalent revenue-based financing if terms preserve control. Triggered only if (a) proof signals are met and (b) a specific opportunity exists that capital meaningfully accelerates. Operator angels means people who've built relevant companies and bring meaningful network and expertise. Founder-friendly terms only: no preferred shares with control rights, no board seats with veto power, no participation rights that compound.

**Stage 2 (optional): Small seed.** $1M-$3M for 15-20%. Triggered only if accelerating enterprise pull is strategic and the unit economics on enterprise are clear. Must preserve founder voting control. Likely Horizon 2 to early Horizon 3.

**Stage 3+: Series A and beyond.** Only if and when scaling on founder's terms with real revenue and real proof. Default assumption: no Series A unless something specific changes the calculus. The company is built to be profitable and sustainable without it.

**Mission-aligned pricing tier.** Subsidized pricing tier within the for-profit company for mission-aligned customers (under-resourced institutions, education, cultural). Deferred to Horizon 3+. Exact structure and qualification criteria TBD.

---

## 6. Team and Hiring Philosophy

**Solo through MVP.** Founder builds alone through Horizon 1. No co-founder pre-MVP. Co-founders before MVP add coordination overhead without proportionate value, and the wrong co-founder is harder to remove than they are to add.

**Skills founder covers:** Engineering, data and ML, product strategy, enterprise sales motion (sales engineering, not pure sales), and story direction.

**Identified gaps:**

- World-class visual design and animation.
- Professional narrative craft at scale.
- Marketing and community, especially developer marketing.

### Sequencing

**Horizon 1.** Default to contractors for visual design, narrative writing, marketing, and specialty technical skills. Equity-bearing collaborators are an exception, evaluated case-by-case with deliberate written justification, vesting schedule, and reverse-vesting clause.

**Horizon 2 (post-MVP, gated by proof signals).** First real co-founder or senior hire. Role to be decided based on which gap is most painful when proof signals hit (creative director, technical co-founder, or GTM co-founder are the candidate roles). Decision is made deliberately before talking to candidates, not while talking to them.

**Horizon 2-3.** Subsequent hires based on which proof signals are strongest at the time.

### Hiring principles

- Hire only when a specific gap is demonstrably blocking progress.
- Prefer contractors over employees in Horizon 1 to preserve optionality and capital efficiency.
- Hire for craft conviction, not for resume.
- All early hires should be aligned on the founder-controlled philosophy.
- Equity for early hires reflects contribution risk and timing, not standard tables.

---

## 7. Proof Signal Framework

The two-axis framework for go/no-go decisions on going full-time and Horizon transitions.

### Product signals (any 2 of 3)

**Build proof.** MVP is shipped, working, and stable enough for real use. Not just demoable; actually playable end-to-end with real groups.

**Use proof.** 5+ live sessions with real groups (not friends-and-family) where the session is finished and the group expresses genuine, unprompted enthusiasm. "It worked" is not enough; "they wanted more" is the bar.

**Pull proof.** Someone outside the immediate circle wants in. An unsolicited request to play, to be early-access, to partner, or to buy. Pull means demand is reaching toward the company, not the other way around. A first-channel hypothesis must be formulated and tested before any public launch: the specific channel expected to generate pull (likely social video demos of real sessions in progress, niche community embeds in game-night and mystery enthusiast communities, and founder-led direct outreach to hosts). The specific channel must be tested before public launch, not after.

### Business signals (any 2 of 3)

**Willingness-to-pay signal.** Real money paid, or clearly offered with concrete intent. Free trials, "I'd love to try it," and Kickstarter-style pre-orders without commitment do not count. Preferred H1 monetization model: host-pays-per-session or host-buys-a-session-credit-pack. Individual player subscriptions are deferred. The willingness-to-pay signal should be tested with the host-pays model at a price point that exceeds the ~$30 static murder mystery kit alternative, since that is the primary price anchor in the consumer category.

**Enterprise conversation signal.** 3+ discovery calls with prospective enterprise buyers, with at least one explicit "I would pilot this." Not "interesting concept," not "let's talk again." A specific pilot intent.

**Inbound signal.** Something organic happened that wasn't manufactured. A press mention, an unsolicited intro, a community post, a developer asking for the API. A thing that came to you, not a thing you caused.

### Decision rule

**Going full-time:** Trigger when 2 of 3 product signals AND 2 of 3 business signals are achieved. Both categories must hit; one is not enough.

**Horizon 1 to Horizon 2 transition:** Same base criteria as going full-time, plus Horizon 2-specific signals (TBD; likely includes second product in development and first paying enterprise customer). Going full-time and entering Horizon 2 are not necessarily the same event; there is a window of full-time-but-still-Horizon-1 where the founder works full-time on the existing wedge before earning the right to expand scope.

**Horizon 2 to Horizon 3+ transition:** Combination of (a) external developer adoption, (b) recurring revenue, and (c) enterprise contract value. Specific thresholds TBD.

### Implicit corollary

Partial signals after 12 months are data, not failure. The honest read is either (a) the product needs more iteration, (b) the market is different than hypothesized, or (c) the part-time pace is the bottleneck. Each has different implications. Monthly review is where this gets evaluated.

---

## 8. Tool Stack and Workflow

**Project chats ([Claude.ai](http://Claude.ai)):** Strategic conversations, planning, analysis, story development, technical design. All foundational artifacts produced and refined here. Default surface for everything pre-implementation.

**Claude Code (terminal-based):** Introduced once implementation begins, roughly after Chat 5 (Technical Architecture) produces the technical design document. Used for engine, games, and production code. Project knowledge artifacts are not auto-shared with Claude Code; reference manually or keep relevant artifacts as markdown in the repo. Decisions made during coding that affect strategy or architecture get surfaced back to the relevant Project chat and updated in the corresponding artifact.

**Cowork:** Not in active use. Reconsider only if a specific non-technical operational pain emerges later (Year 2+ if at all).

### Other tools in stack

- **Source of truth for documents:** Notion (this workspace).
- **Code editor:** Claude Code or Cursor (TBD when implementation starts).
- **Version control:** GitHub.
- **Task tracking:** Linear or GitHub Projects (TBD when build starts).
- **CRM:** TBD when enterprise outreach begins (HubSpot free tier likely).

### Artifact discipline

Every Project artifact has a canonical version in this Notion workspace. When updates happen in a chat, they are reflected here and re-uploaded to Project knowledge. Decisions Log is append-only.

"Six behavior commitments for AI characters (stochastic generation, initiative, NPC-NPC, goal pursuit, per-character profile, arc-level variability)","May 7, 2026","(1) Behavior is generated not scripted (non-zero temperature, character voice). (2) Initiative scheduler: AI characters act unprompted based on goals and state. (3) NPC-to-NPC interactions are first-class. (4) Goal pursuit drives behavior, not just colors it. (5) Per-character behavior_profile JSONB column captures initiative threshold, goal pursuit weight, interaction style, variability. (6) Arc-level variability through non-deterministic decision points. These prevent over-predictability and support 'you had to be there' north star.",Cross-cutting,Committed,

Primary database: Cloud SQL PostgreSQL,"May 7, 2026","In-region with Cloud Run (no cross-cloud latency). Real PostgreSQL with full extension support (pgvector, AGE if needed). $300 GCP free credits cover ~20 months of minimum config. Neon initially recommended but rejected: AWS-only as of May 2026, cross-cloud latency penalty 30-40ms per query. Migration to Neon possible if/when GCP support ships.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Build sequence philosophy: hybrid (build for Nightcap, design platform-clean from day one)","May 7, 2026","Build only what Nightcap needs at MVP, but design every interface as platform-clean from line one. Avoids over-engineering a full platform pre-proof while preventing the 'extract platform later' anti-pattern. Forces discipline on layer separation. Alternatives considered: platform-first (too speculative for solo founder), Nightcap-only with later extraction (creates technical debt that becomes rewrites).",Cross-cutting,Committed,
Authentication: Firebase Auth (dashboard) plus API keys (developers) plus short-lived JWTs (game clients),"May 7, 2026","Three auth surfaces, three patterns. Firebase Auth handles dashboard human logins (GCP-native, free tier 50K MAU, includes password reset and MFA). API keys for developer backend code calling our API (industry standard). Short-lived JWTs for game clients authenticating to a specific session (issued at session start, scoped, expirable). Saves weeks of building auth flows from scratch.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Testing: focused unit tests on knowledge graph, arc engine, safety, model routing","May 7, 2026","Solo founder plus Claude Code primary developer plus MVP scope means full TDD too slow and manual-only too risky. "Arc structure: graph with branching, convergence, multiple endings, loops","May 7, 2026","Arcs are not linear sequences. Beats are nodes; transitions are conditional edges. Graph supports: branching (multiple paths from a beat), convergence (multiple paths into a beat), loops (repeating beats like investigation rounds), multiple terminals (different endings), conditional transitions evaluated at runtime. World mutability supported through state JSONB on locations and objects. Arc mutation at runtime architecturally possible (data-driven YAML, not compiled), implementation deferred until use case requires it.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Content safety: three-layer at MVP, Layer 4 deferred with watchpoint","May 7, 2026","Layer 1: deterministic hard stops (regex blocklists for absolute prohibited content). Layer 2: GPT-OSS-Safeguard 20B on Groq for pre-generation classification, with arc-defined policy (bring-your-own-policy). Layer 3: main LLM with policy in system prompt. Layer 4 (post-generation safety) deferred with watchpoint to add if real sessions surface output problems. Saves one safety call per turn at MVP. Murder mystery genre adjacent to dark content makes Layer 2 essential. GPT-OSS-Safeguard replaces deprecated Llama Guard 4 (Feb 2026 on Groq).",Cross-cutting,Committed,
generation_logs full content population gated behind CONTENT_LOGGING_ENABLED feature flag (default false); non-PII fields populated at MVP,"May 11, 2026","Player-submitted content (names, character choices, dialogue) may appear in generation prompts. "Provenance chains adopted as first-class knowledge graph feature: every knowledge state record tracks why a character knows something, not just what they know","May 11, 2026","Provenance chains (ordered list of character IDs from original source to current knower) enable contradiction detection, realistic 'I heard from someone that...' dialogue, deception modeling via confidence scores, and richer telemetry. Characters with short chains speak with certainty; characters at the end of long chains express appropriate uncertainty. Added to knowledge_states schema as provenance_chain JSONB array with confidence float. No schema migration required to use; it is present from day one.",Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
"Dramatic tension score adopted as unified first-class session metric driving pacing, misdirection, and model tier selection simultaneously","May 11, 2026","A single composite float (0.0-1.0) computed from time pressure, player action rate, correct suspicion confidence, and clue coverage eliminates three separate threshold systems and creates a cleaner architecture. When tension peaks, the routing layer automatically upgrades character dialogue to premium tier without any explicit call-site code. Weights are arc-configurable in pacing_config, enabling iteration without code changes.",Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap

"Balance principle is an engine-enforced constraint: clue chain always sufficient for full investigator engagement, interference throttled against balance state","May 15, 2026","The session must remain genuinely winnable for both sides at all times. "Killer revelation is mid-session, variable between beats 2-4. Killer assignment and killer revelation are two distinct events.","May 15, 2026",Killer does not know they are the killer at session start. Assignment fires internally at any point from session start to just before revelation. Engine observes player behavior passively and can be accelerated by specific interaction triggers. Revelation fires privately on killer device at assigned beat (range 2-4). This produces authentic early-game investigative behavior and a strategic pivot moment when revelation lands. Differentiates Nightcap from all major imposter-format games.,Cross-cutting,Committed,

D-048 M0 Wizard-of-Oz validation gate overridden,"May 2026","PRD v1.3 Section 9 defined a manual Wizard-of-Oz facilitation phase (minimum 10 sessions, personalization perception signal required in 2+) as a required gate before significant production engineering. This gate is explicitly overridden. The founder's build sequence is: Engine, Platform, Game, live test with real users, iterate. No game exists yet and no one has played a session. Validation of the personalization thesis will happen through real-user qualifying sessions at M6, not a pre-engineering simulation phase. The personalization thesis is treated as a working hypothesis to be confirmed or disproved by the real product in real users' hands. This is consistent with the PRD's explicit founder-override provision. Risk accepted: production engineering begins before the personalization layer has been validated with real users. If M6 live testing reveals the personalization thesis does not hold, more engineering will need to be revisited than if a WoZ phase had surfaced this earlier. Founder accepts this tradeoff explicitly.",Process / MVP,Committed,"M0, validation, wizard-of-oz, MVP, override, personalization"
D-049 GitHub Projects and Issues is the primary project tracker for the Arcwright build,"May 2026","Code, AI agents (Claude Code, Codex, Copilot), and task tracking live in one place. Agents can read issues, execute against them, open PRs, and close issues via commit message references natively. No integration bridge is required between code and tracker. GitHub sub-issues and milestones support the roadmap's milestone, epic, and task hierarchy. Zero admin overhead for a solo founder. Linear and Jira were considered and rejected: Linear adds context-switching cost without proportionate benefit at this team size; Jira is designed for multi-team process governance that does not yet exist. Revisit trigger: first non-technical co-founder or PM hire who needs richer reporting or lives in a different tool.",Process / Tooling,Committed,"tooling, project-management, github, planning"
D-050 Nightcap game UI will be built on an external platform connecting to Arcwright via API,"May 2026","The Nightcap experience layer (host interface, player interface) will be delivered via a third-party platform that connects to Arcwright through its API, rather than Arcwright building those surfaces directly. M1 through M3 are unaffected because they are backend and API only. Append-only event log captures all changes (telemetry, replay, audit, recovery for free). In-memory cache during active sessions for sub-millisecond reads. Stack positioning: Arcwright is narrative runtime middleware (Layer 2 in game dev stack),"May 7, 2026","Arcwright sits between game engines (Unity, Unreal, Godot, web) and AI providers (Anthropic, OpenAI, Groq). Engine handles rendering, input, audio. Arcwright handles arc orchestration, characters, knowledge state, content events. AI providers handle generation. Engine-agnostic and provider-agnostic. Closest analogue: http://Charisma.ai (more controllable, character-level vs session-level). Differentiated from: Convai (3D-native lock-in), Inworld (pivoted), Latitude/Voyage (consumer not platform), Ink/Articy (authored not generative).",Cross-cutting,Committed,

"Six behavior commitments for AI characters (stochastic generation, initiative, NPC-NPC, goal pursuit, per-character profile, arc-level variability)","May 7, 2026","(1) Behavior is generated not scripted (non-zero temperature, character voice). (2) Initiative scheduler: AI characters act unprompted based on goals and state. (3) NPC-to-NPC interactions are first-class. (4) Goal pursuit drives behavior, not just colors it. (5) Per-character behavior_profile JSONB column captures initiative threshold, goal pursuit weight, interaction style, variability. (6) Arc-level variability through non-deterministic decision points. These prevent over-predictability and support 'you had to be there' north star.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Arc execution engine: event-driven coordinator with Python asyncio plus python-statemachine v3, graph traversal","May 7, 2026","Engine is event-driven coordinator: in-process pub/sub via asyncio, components subscribe and emit. python-statemachine v3.0 (Feb 2026) handles beat progression as graph traversal (branching, convergence, multiple endings, loops). Best fit for concurrent concerns (beat, pacing, initiative, character behavior, safety). Lowest engine overhead for player-perceived latency. Temporal rejected: heavyweight workflow engine designed for long-running cross-service durability, overkill for solo founder MVP with hour-long sessions.",Cross-cutting,Committed,

"Arc structure: graph with branching, convergence, multiple endings, loops","May 7, 2026","Arcs are not linear sequences. Beats are nodes; transitions are conditional edges. Graph supports: branching (multiple paths from a beat), convergence (multiple paths into a beat), loops (repeating beats like investigation rounds), multiple terminals (different endings), conditional transitions evaluated at runtime. Layer 4 (post-generation safety) deferred with watchpoint to add if real sessions surface output problems. Saves one safety call per turn at MVP. "Provenance chains adopted as first-class knowledge graph feature: every knowledge state record tracks why a character knows something, not just what they know","May 11, 2026","Provenance chains (ordered list of character IDs from original source to current knower) enable contradiction detection, realistic 'I heard from someone that...' dialogue, deception modeling via confidence scores, and richer telemetry. Characters with short chains speak with certainty; characters at the end of long chains express appropriate uncertainty. Added to knowledge_states schema as provenance_chain JSONB array with confidence float. No schema migration required to use; it is present from day one.",Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
"Dramatic tension score adopted as unified first-class session metric driving pacing, misdirection, and model tier selection simultaneously","May 11, 2026","A single composite float (0.0-1.0) computed from time pressure, player action rate, correct suspicion confidence, and clue coverage eliminates three separate threshold systems and creates a cleaner architecture. When tension peaks, the routing layer automatically upgrades character dialogue to premium tier without any explicit call-site code. Weights are arc-configurable in pacing_config, enabling iteration without code changes.",Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
python-statemachine v3.0 StateChart confirmed as arc execution library; StateChart base class (not StateMachine) is correct,"May 11, 2026","Verified May 11 2026 that v3.0 supports all required arc graph patterns: parallel regions (State.Parallel), compound states (State.Compound), history states, delayed events, conditional transitions via cond=, and invoked sub-machines. The StateChart base class is the SCXML-compliant class introduced in v3.0; StateMachine is the legacy v2.x-compatible class and must not be used. NightcapArcChart implements investigation beat as State.Parallel so private clue distribution and group interrogation run simultaneously.",Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
"Nightcap character mode: generated. Characters are generated per session from typed character slots, not from authored fixed definitions. Character identities, names, and personalities are generated at session start, calibrated to the specific player group.","May 14, 2026","Every session should feel like a genuinely different story (Miracle Workers / Glass Onion model). Fixed authored characters produce a recognizable cast that repeats, reducing replayability. The arc schema supports authored, generated, and hybrid modes at the platform level; Nightcap uses generated.",Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
"Nightcap setting constraint: social gathering. The physical construct of every Nightcap session is some kind of social gathering. Time period, tone, and specific setting vary within this constraint.","May 14, 2026",Players should not need heavy imaginative lifting to inhabit the world. Social gathering is something all players have real-world experience with. Time period and accent can vary freely. Exotic settings with no player reference point break immersion rather than building it.,Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
"Nightcap aesthetic mode: generative. The visual and tonal aesthetic of each session is generated fresh. The platform supports fixed, palette, and generative aesthetic modes; Nightcap uses generative.","May 14, 2026",Generative aesthetics contribute to session unrepeatability. Future arcs can use any mode.,Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
Nightcap play mode at MVP: imposter. One player is assigned the killer role at session start and plays to avoid detection. All other players are investigators. The killer receives a fundamentally different private phone experience from all other players.,"May 14, 2026","Imposter mode creates the strongest social dynamics for a group party game: paranoia, misdirection, alliance-forming, and accusation. The killer's private experience maps directly to the personalization engine's strength. Replay value is high because the killer role is randomly assigned each session. Detective race mode deferred to v1.1.",Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
Nightcap arc structure: Dan Harmon Story Circle. Arc structure is a configurable platform-level parameter; Nightcap uses Dan Harmon.,"May 14, 2026","The Story Circle maps cleanly onto a murder mystery: normal world, disruption (murder), investigation, revelation, return transformed. Man in a Hole works for individual player emotional arcs within a session and can coexist at that level.",Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
"Nightcap narrator: host persona on shared display. Voiced character on the TV. Aesthetic-linked persona, omniscient, player-addressable. Not a murder suspect. Behavior triggers: beat transitions, clue releases, tension threshold, player inaction. Mostly absent from phones.","May 14, 2026",The narrator is the architect of the evening: the host who built the stage and knows everything. The TV is the social anchor all players share when dispersed on phones. Persona adapts to aesthetic (dry Victorian butler vs theatrical Italian host) contributing to unrepeatability. Not a competing detective but an all-knowing master of ceremonies.,Cross-cutting,Committed,roadmap
Story Circle is a functional platform-native 8-beat template (not decorative metadata),"May 15, 2026","arc_structure field value changed from dan_harmon to story_circle. Story Circle is now a first-class platform object that scaffolds 8 pre-populated beat containers with story_circle_step, structural_function, and suggested dramatic_purpose. arc_structure is a functional engine input used for generation context, pacing calibration, and structural intent. Authors using Story Circle get pre-scaffolded beats; custom arc authors define their own. Resolved the open architecture question from Chat 7 pre-work.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Killer active capabilities are story-prompted optional actions, not tracked resource pools","May 15, 2026","No ability_charge concept. The engine identifies when a story moment makes an action narratively appropriate and presents it as an optional prompt on the killer device. Killer accepts or declines. Story continues either way. The killer's experience is being a character in a story, not managing a hand of cards. Ability_pool concept in arc definition now means the set of action types available in this session, not a resource counter.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
Session duration is emergent (30-75 min target range). No separate speed round mode.,"May 15, 2026","Speed round is a fast group plus responsive pacing engine, not a designed configuration. Duration range replaces any session_mode parameter. The pacing engine manages within the 30-75 minute range based on player behavior. Both ends of the range are valid session outcomes.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Nightcap uses 8 execution beats in 1:1 Story Circle mapping: The Arrival, The Body, The Opening Move, The Dig, The Thread, The Reckoning, The Close, The Truth","May 15, 2026","8 beats gives the engine direct knowledge of the current Story Circle phase at all times, enabling structural intent injection into generation, tone-aware pacing, and ensemble coordination. Named beats are Nightcap-canonical labels, separate from the Story Circle step names. BeatDefinition schema expanded with story_circle_step, structural_function, dramatic_purpose, emotional_target, information_goal, tension_target, character_emphasis.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
aesthetic_mode replaced by aesthetic_config with per-element generation strategies. tone_config added to arc definition.,"May 15, 2026","Aesthetic has four categories: host-selectable (era + occasion, with Pick for Me option), pre-produced per theme (backgrounds, music, animations, UI), generated at session start (character portraits), and generative runtime (all text/narrative). Pre-produced is the v1 implementation; runtime generation is a planned A/B experiment. tone_config has brand_envelope (outer bounds per dimension), scenario_defaults (dial positions), and voice_directive (free text). Nightcap brand envelope: irreverence 0.5-1.0, suspense 0.4-0.9, dark comedy 0.4-0.85, wit density 0.6-1.0, chaos tolerance 0.3-0.8.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Fully generative story content is a Nightcap-specific design decision, not a platform requirement","May 15, 2026","The Arcwright platform supports authored, generative, and hybrid content strategies per arc. Nightcap chose fully generative story elements (characters, murder, clues, dialogue). Other arcs may have fixed authored characters, authored story content with generative edges, or any other combination. This distinction must be explicit in all platform documentation to avoid miscommunicating platform capabilities as Nightcap design choices.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
Victim is a dedicated 7th structural position. Killer designates victim at revelation. Eligibility governed by player count (threshold: 4+ human players for player-eligible).,"May 15, 2026","Victim slot is separate from the 6 player role types. In standard player counts (under threshold), victim is NPC. With 4+ human players, a human can be designated. The killer selects from available characters at the moment of revelation. Victim player receives their own private revelation with role assignment from the victim role pool: Witness, Specter, Informant, or Conspirator (conditional). All victim roles keep the player engaged through Beat 8. All learn killer identity at Beat 8 with everyone else.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Balance principle is an engine-enforced constraint: clue chain always sufficient for full investigator engagement, interference throttled against balance state","May 15, 2026","The session must remain genuinely winnable for both sides at all times. Genuine clue chain has enough redundancy that no single interference event makes the case unsolvable. Killer interference opportunities are throttled against the session balance state. False clues are always falsifiable given the complete genuine evidence set. This principle governs clue distribution, puzzle gating, and killer action opportunity surfacing.",Cross-cutting,Committed,
"Killer revelation is mid-session, variable between beats 2-4. Killer assignment and killer revelation are two distinct events.","May 15, 2026",Killer does not know they are the killer at session start. Assignment fires internally at any point from session start to just before revelation. Engine observes player behavior passively and can be accelerated by specific interaction triggers. Revelation fires privately on killer device at assigned beat (range 2-4). This produces authentic early-game investigative behavior and a strategic pivot moment when revelation lands. Differentiates Nightcap from all major imposter-format games.,Cross-cutting,Committed,
Murder timing is variable across beats 1-3. Mini-games active in beats 1-3 feed killer assignment logic.,"May 15, 2026","Murder can occur in any of the first three beats, not at a fixed narrative point. This mimics real social dynamics and creates meaningfully different session experiences. Mini-games (Jackbox-style social games) are framed as part of the gathering and run in beats 1-3. Their behavioral outputs are named inputs to the killer assignment logic. Players have no visibility into this function.",Cross-cutting,Committed,

## SOURCE FILE: docs/02-Decisions-Log-Additions-May2026.md

# Decisions Log Additions, May 2026

**Merge target:** 02-Decisions-Log (append-only; add these entries at the end)
**Produced in:** Build planning session, May 2026

---

## Entry 1

**Decision:** M0 Wizard-of-Oz validation gate overridden
**Date:** May 2026
**Rationale:** PRD v1.3 Section 9 defined a manual Wizard-of-Oz facilitation phase (minimum 10 sessions, personalization perception signal required in 2+) as a required gate before significant production engineering. This gate is explicitly overridden. The founder's build sequence is: Engine, Platform, Game, live test with real users, iterate. No game exists yet and no one has played a session. Validation of the personalization thesis will happen through real-user qualifying sessions at M6, not a pre-engineering simulation phase. The personalization thesis is treated as a working hypothesis to be confirmed or disproved by the real product in real users' hands. This is consistent with the PRD's explicit founder-override provision.
**Risk accepted:** Production engineering begins before the personalization layer has been validated with real users. If M6 live testing reveals the personalization thesis does not hold, more engineering will need to be revisited than if a WoZ phase had surfaced this earlier. Founder accepts this tradeoff explicitly.
**Status:** Active. Logged May 2026.
**Section:** Process / MVP
**Tags:** M0, validation, wizard-of-oz, MVP, override, personalization

---

## Entry 2

**Decision:** GitHub Projects and Issues is the primary project tracker for the Arcwright build
**Date:** May 2026
**Rationale:** Code, AI agents (Claude Code, Codex, Copilot), and task tracking live in one place. Agents can read issues, execute against them, open PRs, and close issues via commit message references natively. No integration bridge required between code and tracker. GitHub sub-issues (GA) and milestones support the roadmap's milestone, epic, and task hierarchy. Zero admin overhead for a solo founder. Linear and Jira were considered and rejected: Linear adds context-switching cost without proportionate benefit at this team size; Jira is designed for multi-team process governance that does not yet exist.
**Revisit trigger:** First non-technical co-founder or PM hire who needs richer reporting or lives in a different tool.
**Status:** Active.
**Section:** Process / Tooling
**Tags:** tooling, project-management, github, planning

---

## Entry 3

**Decision:** Nightcap game UI will be built on an external platform connecting to Arcwright via API; not built directly by Arcwright
**Date:** May 2026
**Rationale:** Founder confirmed the Nightcap experience layer (host interface, player interface) will be delivered via a third-party platform that connects to the Arcwright platform through its API, rather than Arcwright building those surfaces directly. This is consistent with the PRD surface-agnosticism principle: the engine emits content events tagged with context; the experience layer renders them. The specific external platform is not yet named.
**Implication for roadmap:** M4 (Nightcap experience layer) task decomposition is deferred until the external platform is selected. The platform choice drives what SDK or integration tasks are required. M1 through M3 are unaffected; they are backend and API only.
**Status:** Active. Platform TBD; revisit when M3 nears its exit gate.
**Section:** Product / Architecture
**Tags:** M4, Nightcap, experience-layer, surface-agnosticism, platform

---

*End of additions. Do not edit earlier entries. Append only.*

---

"Open source self-hosting break-even (Chat 6 deliverable, RESOLVED)",Product,"May 7, 2026","May 7, 2026",High,"Calculated in Chat 6a (May 7, 2026). ## SOURCE FILE: docs/04-Naming-and-Brand-v1 2 356b7de354a88132aa7bdf4907fd4f25.md

# 04-Naming-and-Brand-v1.2

**Version:** 1.2

**Last Updated:** May 2026

**Status:** Living document — v1.2 Chat 9 soft bifurcation update applied via Notion connector (May 2026)

---

## Chat 9 Brand Architecture Update

Brand approach is soft bifurcation: one legal entity, two product brands inside it. Arcwright is the platform-facing identity for developers and enterprise. Arcwright Studios is the consumer-facing publishing label for games. Platform-facing web properties, documentation, enterprise contracts, and developer materials lead with Arcwright. Studio brand appears on game splash screens, App Store and Steam pages, consumer site, and press for game releases. Specific legal entity name remains deferred to legal-formation work with counsel.

Visual Storyworld is the internal name for visual creator tooling. Treat it as a potential trademark only if it becomes external-facing.

## 1. Final Name Selections

| Item | Name | Status |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Platform | Arcwright | Committed |
| Studio / publishing sub-brand | Arcwright Studios | Committed as consumer-facing publishing label |
| Company (legal entity) | Arcwright or counsel-approved variant | Deferred to legal formation |
| Game (murder mystery) | Nightcap | Pending trademark counsel clearance |
| Game fallback | Revel | Committed if Nightcap fails clearance |
| Game (monster RPG) | TBD | Deferred to Chat 8 (Story Bible: Monster RPG) |

---

## 2. Naming Reasoning

### Platform: Arcwright

Arcwright is a compound coinword: arc (narrative arc, structural span, precision) plus wright (craftsperson, as in playwright, wheelwright). Distinctive and ownable, carries craft and making imagery, earns its meaning over time rather than explaining itself upfront, and scales across all verticals and horizons without implying a single category. Passed all eight due-diligence checks with no blocking conflicts. The pretentiousness flag (the wright suffix is not universally known) was raised and consciously accepted.

### Brand Architecture: Soft Bifurcation

Arcwright is the platform-facing identity. Arcwright Studios is the consumer-facing publishing label for games. This absorbs the B2B trust concern around the Studios suffix without forcing premature legal or operational complexity. The company should not sell developer API infrastructure or enterprise products primarily under a Studios-only identity once those conversations begin. Legal entity name is deferred to counsel; operationally, the brand system treats Arcwright as platform and Arcwright Studios as studio label.

**Trademark strategy:** two filings under one entity: platform-facing brand under Class 9 or 42 (computer software), studio brand under Class 41 (entertainment).

### Game: Nightcap (pending clearance)

Retained as working title pending formal trademark counsel review. Two material conflicts identified: Studio Nightcap (active indie game studio in Pittsburgh making a murder mystery game) and NBA Nightcap (Amazon Prime Video, Class 41 entertainment). Counsel must clear or reject before any public launch materials use the name. Fallback committed: Revel.

### Game fallback: Revel

Selected for warmth, social energy, and clean conflict landscape. Revel is the party where the murder happens. Single word, adult, group-play energy. Still requires counsel review before launch, but no blocking conflicts found in initial research.

**Descriptor note:** Revel communicates party energy clearly but does not communicate mystery or whodunit format on its own. If Revel is activated as the primary name, consumer-facing marketing should pair it with a consistent subtitle or descriptor that communicates genre and format at first contact. Working examples: "Revel: The Murder Mystery Party" or "Revel: A Murder Mystery Game." The descriptor should be locked before any public launch materials are produced under the Revel name.

---

## 3. Finalists Considered Per Item

### Platform name finalists (due diligence completed)

**Arcwright** (selected): No blocking conflicts. [arcwright.com](http://arcwright.com), [arcwright.ai](http://arcwright.ai), [arcwright.io](http://arcwright.io) appear unregistered. Social handles available. Clean linguistic and cultural check. Arcwright Fabworks (Arkansas metal fabrication) and Arkwright Consulting (management consulting) are phonetically adjacent but different class entirely. Arcweave (narrative design tool) shares the Arc prefix but is a different name.

**Narrata** (eliminated): [narrat.dev](http://narrat.dev) is an active open-source narrative game engine with established developer community. One letter apart, same space, phonetically nearly identical. Common law conflict highly probable.

**Lore** (eliminated as platform name): Used generically throughout gaming. Trademark registration in Class 41/42 would be extremely difficult. Multiple active brands in the space.

**PlotForge** (eliminated): [plotforge.app](http://plotforge.app) is an active AI-powered creative writing platform (Loophead Labs LLC). [plotforge.io](http://plotforge.io) is an active AI D&D session prep tool. [theplotforge.com](http://theplotforge.com) is an active story writing platform. Three active competitors using the exact name.

### Game name candidates

**Nightcap** (conditionally retained): Conflicts: Studio Nightcap (Pittsburgh indie studio, murder mystery genre); NBA Nightcap (Amazon Prime, Class 41). Pending counsel clearance.

**Last Call** (eliminated): LAST CALL Murder Mystery Party Game is an active product at [aneveningofmurder.com](http://aneveningofmurder.com). Direct category match.

**Guilty Party** (requires counsel if pursued): Disney Interactive 2011 Wii murder mystery party game. Same genre. Disney Interactive Studios was shut down; trademark may have lapsed but not confirmed. Not selected as fallback.

**Revel** (fallback committed): No blocking conflicts found.

---

## 4. Names Considered and Rejected (Full List)

Platform candidates eliminated in candidate rounds: Motif, Kairos, Tessera, Fable, Thread, Fabula, Cadence, Volta, Mythos, Eidos, Limn, Scroll, Codex, Parable, Narratica, Storysmith. Reasons: taste filter (most), scope concerns (Lore), conflict (Narrata, PlotForge).

Game candidates eliminated: Last Call (active conflict), Guilty Party (Disney conflict, unconfirmed lapse).

---

## 5. Trademark Filing Checklist

| Item | Class | Priority | Status | Notes |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Arcwright (platform) | 9 or 42 (computer software/SaaS) | High | Not filed | File before public platform/developer launch; counsel to confirm class strategy |
| Arcwright (platform) | 41 (entertainment services) | High | Not filed | File alongside Class 42 |
| Arcwright Studios (studio sub-brand) | 41 (entertainment) | High | Not filed | Publishing/studio label filing under same entity |
| Nightcap (game) | 41 (entertainment), 9 (software) | Critical | Blocked | Requires counsel clearance before filing |
| Revel (fallback) | 41, 9 | Medium | Not filed | File only if Nightcap fails clearance |
| Visual Storyworld | 9 or 42 if external-facing | Low | Not filed | Internal tooling name only for now; consider filing only if external-facing |

**Timing recommendation:** Engage trademark counsel before MVP launch. Clearance opinion costs $500 to $2,000. Filing costs $250 to $350 per class per mark via USPTO TEAS Plus. Do not wait until launch.

**Recommended approach:** Engage a trademark attorney directly for Nightcap clearance given the known conflicts. For Arcwright, a service like Markify or Trademarkia can run an initial search; attorney review before filing.

---

## 6. Domain Registration Priority List

Register in this order. All treated as urgent.

1. [arcwright.com](http://arcwright.com) (highest priority, register immediately)
2. [arcwright.ai](http://arcwright.ai) (register immediately alongside .com)
3. [arcwright.io](http://arcwright.io) (register immediately)
4. [arcwrightstudios.com](http://arcwrightstudios.com) (company identity, register immediately)
5. [arcwright.co](http://arcwright.co) (defensive)
6. [arcwright.games](http://arcwright.games) (register before launch)
7. [arcwright.studio](http://arcwright.studio) (defensive, register before launch)
8. [playnightcap.com](http://playnightcap.com) (conditional on name clearance, register before game launch)
9. [revelgame.com](http://revelgame.com) or [playwithrevel.com](http://playwithrevel.com) (fallback insurance, register now)

---

## 7. Social Handle Reservation Priority List

Claim all immediately, before any public announcement.

**Arcwright Studios (company and platform):**

- X/Twitter: @arcwright or @arcwrightstudios
- Instagram: @arcwrightstudios
- TikTok: @arcwrightstudios
- YouTube: @arcwrightstudios
- GitHub: arcwright (organization)
- LinkedIn: company page as Arcwright Studios
- Discord: Arcwright Studios server (claim before public launch)
