## SOURCE FILE: docs/prd/03-scope.md

> Source: Project knowledge artifact 06-PRD-v1.3
> Last synced: 2026-05-21
> Do not edit this file directly; edit in Notion and re-sync.

# Scope

## MVP Definition and Milestone Map

**Scope clarity:** "Platform MVP" at this stage means the internal engine that runs Nightcap, with architecture clean and documented enough that a technical co-founder joining post-MVP can understand every decision without a guided tour. It is not an externally packaged API product, not a polished developer-facing service, and not a platform open to third-party developers. The done-criterion "documented well enough for a technical co-founder" means internal architecture documentation, not a public developer experience. This distinction determines where build time goes during H1.

**MVP is done when all of the following are true:** Nightcap is playable end-to-end by a group of 4-10 real players not involved in building it. The session completes through all three beats including the reveal. Knowledge state enforcement works. Session persistence works. The provider-agnostic model routing abstraction layer is in place. Structured session telemetry is live logging minimum required signals. The platform API is documented well enough for a technical co-founder to read the architecture without explanation. AI credit tracking is live and the founder knows per-session gross margin at each player count. Content safety rails are active. At least one arc schema other than Nightcap has been designed. At least one adversarial playtest round has been completed, specifically designed to probe content safety rails, dark-content edge cases, and player attempts to break tone, embarrass other players, or inject prohibited content; results reviewed and blocking issues resolved before first real-user sessions begin. The solo-founder critical path has been honored: the developer-facing dashboard and arc authoring interface are the lowest-priority MVP components and are deferred until the consumer experience is validated; the critical path for solo delivery is arc execution engine, session management, knowledge graph, Nightcap game integration, safety rails, basic cost tracking, and structured telemetry.

**H3+ North Star:** Arcwright is platform-first. External developers ship experiences on the infrastructure. Tier 2 proprietary infrastructure is active for at least some model call categories.

**H2 gate:** External developer closed beta opens only after two gate conditions are met: at least five external developers are building non-Nightcap experiences and Nightcap has produced a profitability signal. The specific profitability threshold (revenue level, unit economics, recurring revenue, or combined signal) is deferred until Nightcap pricing is set. Monster RPG shipped or in final development. Enterprise team-building product has at least one paying customer. Recurring platform revenue exists independent of game sales. Tier 2 fine-tuning viability assessed against accumulated telemetry data.

**H2 milestones:** Monster RPG shipped. Enterprise team-building product shipped. Third game selected against remaining capability gaps. Platform API stable for external developers. Open source self-hosting break-even calculated against actual H1 session volume and token consumption data. First co-founder or senior hire in place.

**H1 gate:** Two of three product proof signals met and two of three business proof signals met, per the framework in 01-Strategy-Document Section 7.

**Pre-build validation phase (required before significant production code is written):** Before engineering work begins on the production Nightcap system, a manual validation phase must produce qualifying results. This phase uses human-operated orchestration and off-the-shelf tools only; no production code. Minimum 10 facilitated sessions run with a human operator making pacing decisions, selecting clue targeting, and adjusting character behavior in real time. Sessions must include groups not involved in building the product. Minimum 2 sessions must produce the personalization perception signal: at least one player references something specifically calibrated to their group without being prompted. At least one session should use a format other than murder mystery to test whether the personalization effect is thesis-level or genre-level. The gate for entering production engineering is: qualifying sessions complete and personalization perception signal confirmed in at least 2 sessions. Sessions that complete successfully but produce no personalization perception signal require diagnosis before production engineering begins.

**Scope debt:** Dashboard at MVP is developer-facing only and is the first component to cut if time or scope pressure emerges; arc schema documentation and internal API architecture documentation serve the same near-term function at a fraction of the build cost; do not build dashboard polish before the consumer experience is validated. Knowledge graph schema at MVP is simple; extensibility path must be designed now. External developer documentation at MVP is not sufficient for a public API launch. Telemetry schema beyond MVP minimum must be designed in Chat 6. The pre-build Wizard-of-Oz validation phase is not optional scope that can be skipped to save time; skipping it means entering production engineering before knowing whether the personalization layer produces felt results in a real room.

## Visual Storyworld Roadmap

Visual creator tooling, internally referred to as Visual Storyworld, is staged across five phases. Phase 1 ships with platform MVP in H1 and includes inspection-only surfaces: live knowledge graph visualization, read-only arc structure view, live event stream, and character state inspection. Phase 2 ships during H2 prep and adds structured editing of existing primitives, including arc composition, character authoring, and content event templates. Phase 3 ships with H2 launch and adds live preview and runtime debugging. Phase 4 ships H2 mature to H3 early and adds a full visual flow editor. Phase 5 ships H3 plus and may add asset libraries, marketplace if pull exists, and AI-assisted authoring. Positioning is narrative middleware with extraordinary creator tooling, not a no-code platform.

## Business Model Architecture

Arcwright uses four pricing tiers: Free Developer, Indie, Studio, and Enterprise. Free Developer includes limited credits, full API access, rate limits, and prototyping use. Indie is designed for solo and small-team indie studios, with substantial included credits and community support. Studio is designed for studios of 5 to 50 people, with generous credits, priority support, and basic SLA. Enterprise uses custom annual contracts, SLA, eventually SOC 2 when achievable, and white-label or co-brand options. Action credits are abstracted as narrative actions, such as character dialogue generation, beat selection or transition, fate event evaluation, knowledge state query, or arc state update. Numeric prices remain deferred until Nightcap pricing is set.

## SOURCE FILE: docs/prd/04-non-goals.md

> Source: Project knowledge artifact 06-PRD-v1.3
> Last synced: 2026-05-21
> Do not edit this file directly; edit in Notion and re-sync.

# Non-Goals

## What the Platform Must Not Do

- Must not assume a specific delivery surface at the engine layer.
- Must not treat AI as the creative author.
- Must not allow knowledge state management to be skipped or made optional.
- Must not expose model routing decisions or model names to end players.
- Must not hard-code a dependency on any specific AI provider, model, or model version.
- Must not be designed in a way that requires a rebuild to support emergent narrative arcs (monster RPG) or multi-team enterprise sessions.
- Must not launch without content safety architecture active.
- Must not assume a specific team size or build capacity in its requirements.
- Must not include authoring capabilities that only Nightcap needs and classify them as platform capabilities.
- Must not ship without session telemetry instrumented.

## Open Questions and Deferred Decisions

**Critical:** Nightcap trademark clearance (counsel not yet engaged; known conflicts: Studio Nightcap and NBA Nightcap). Domain and social handle registration (urgent action item).

**High:** What does the enterprise team-building product look like as a distinct arc? When does the platform open to external developers and what is the selection process? Which role does the first co-founder fill? Third game selection against platform capability gaps. Open source self-hosting break-even calculation (Chat 6 deliverable). External developer demand validation: before the H2 closed developer beta opens, show the internal API documentation and arc schema format to at least 10 target external developers and record their feedback and pilot intent; the beta should not open on the basis of assumed demand. Enterprise buyer receptiveness: as soon as a working consumer prototype or demo footage exists, conduct brief interviews with 10 enterprise buyers across HR, L&D, and events manager roles using the demo footage; this should happen in H1, not at H2 entry.

**Medium:** Monster RPG arc design (Chat 8). H2-to-H3 transition signal thresholds. Mission-aligned pricing tier structure (H3+). Full telemetry schema design (Chat 6 deliverable).

**Parked:** Adaptive individual learning as future vertical. No-code arc builder for non-developer creators.

# PRD Directory

This directory contains the Product Requirements Document split into focused sections for easier navigation and versioning.

## Files

- **01-overview.md**: Product vision and three-horizon roadmap
- **02-requirements.md**: Architecture principles, Nightcap reference implementation, platform capabilities
- **03-scope.md**: MVP definition, milestone map, Visual Storyworld roadmap, business model
- **04-non-goals.md**: Architectural constraints and deferred decisions

## Adding New PRD Files

- Follow the naming convention: `NN-description.md` (e.g., `05-pricing-model.md`)
- Each file should have a metadata block at the top:
  ```
  > Source: Project knowledge artifact 06-PRD-v1.3
  > Last synced: YYYY-MM-DD
  > Do not edit this file directly; edit in Notion and re-sync.
  ```
- Use H1 headings for main sections
- Link between related files using relative markdown links
- Keep metadata synced when upstream PRD is updated

# Primary database: Cloud SQL PostgreSQL

Date: May 7, 2026
Rationale: In-region with Cloud Run (no cross-cloud latency). Real PostgreSQL with full extension support (pgvector, AGE if needed). $300 GCP free credits cover ~20 months of minimum config. Neon initially recommended but rejected: AWS-only as of May 2026, cross-cloud latency penalty 30-40ms per query. Migration to Neon possible if/when GCP support ships.
Section: Cross-cutting
Status: Committed

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Progressive proprietary infrastructure three-tier  358b7de354a881cebfd6e036c9bedb5a.md

# Progressive proprietary infrastructure: three-tier build sequence (deterministic now, fine-tuned models at scale, foundation models never)

Date: May 5, 2026
Rationale: Tier 1 at MVP: deterministic infrastructure with no AI cost (arc engine, session state, knowledge graph, routing, API). Tier 2 at Horizon 2 earliest, triggered by volume and cost data: fine-tuned open source models. Tier 3, never: foundation model development or compute ownership. Games are the data flywheel; session telemetry from day one is the mechanism. Competitors using the same APIs cannot replicate Arcwright-specific session data. Premature Tier 2 investment before data and economics justify it is a distraction from shipping.
Section: Section 3: Three-Horizon Roadmap
Status: Committed
Tags: capital, pillars, roadmap

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Provenance chains adopted as first-class knowledge 360b7de354a88172b233e94c925d4ef5.md

# Provenance chains adopted as first-class knowledge graph feature: every knowledge state record tracks why a character knows something, not just what they know

Date: May 11, 2026
Rationale: Provenance chains (ordered list of character IDs from original source to current knower) enable contradiction detection, realistic 'I heard from someone that...' dialogue, deception modeling via confidence scores, and richer telemetry. Characters with short chains speak with certainty; characters at the end of long chains express appropriate uncertainty. Added to knowledge_states schema as provenance_chain JSONB array with confidence float. No schema migration required to use; it is present from day one.
Section: Cross-cutting
Status: Committed
Tags: roadmap

---
## SOURCE FILE: docs/Provider-agnostic model routing is a named archite 358b7de354a881e38c06cdb9060c07d1.md

# Provider-agnostic model routing is a named architectural requirement, not an implication

Date: May 5, 2026
Rationale: No platform operation may hard-code a dependency on any specific AI provider or model. All model calls route through an internal abstraction layer. Enables cost optimization through provider switching, compliance flexibility for enterprise customers, and Tier 2 migration from managed APIs to fine-tuned open source models without changing arc execution logic.
Section: Section 2: Strategic Pillars
Status: Committed
Tags: pillars

## SOURCE FILE: docs/python-statemachine v3 0 StateChart confirmed as a 360b7de354a881dbb2f0faa419e7ad83.md

# python-statemachine v3.0 StateChart confirmed as arc execution library; StateChart base class (not StateMachine) is correct

Date: May 11, 2026
Rationale: Verified May 11 2026 that v3.0 supports all required arc graph patterns: parallel regions (State.Parallel), compound states (State.Compound), history states, delayed events, conditional transitions via cond=, and invoked sub-machines. The StateChart base class is the SCXML-compliant class introduced in v3.0; StateMachine is the legacy v2.x-compatible class and must not be used. NightcapArcChart implements investigation beat as State.Parallel so private clue distribution and group interrogation run simultaneously.
Section: Cross-cutting
Status: Committed
Tags: roadmap

## SOURCE FILE: docs/roadmap/00-overview.md

# 12-Build-Roadmap-v1.1

**Version:** 1.1  
**Date:** May 2026  
**Status:** Active  
**Derived from:** 06-PRD-v1.3 and 07-Technical-Architecture-v1.3  
**Primary audiences:** Founder, AI coding agents, future technical co-founder

## How To Use This Roadmap

This is the execution layer beneath the PRD and Technical Architecture.

- The PRD says what and why.
- The Architecture says how the system is shaped.
- This roadmap says what gets built, in what order, by whom, and how each piece is verified.

Three layers:

- **Milestones** group work and end at a verifiable gate.
- **Epics** are coherent chunks of work inside a milestone.
- **Tasks** are sized for a single AI agent session.

Source-of-truth rule: tasks reference Architecture and PRD sections rather than restating schemas. If a task and the Architecture doc disagree, the Architecture doc wins; fix the task.

Decomposition policy: Milestone 1 is complete. AW-201 decomposes Milestones 2 through 6 into epics and agent-sized task specs so the path to first qualifying Nightcap playtests is executable. M4 implementation tasks are anchored to the AW-202 Nightcap web experience runtime decision before runtime-specific work begins.

## M0 Gate Override

PRD v1.3 Section 9 defined a Wizard-of-Oz manual validation phase before significant production code. That gate has been explicitly overridden by the founder.

Build sequence: Engine, Platform, Game, live test with real users, iterate.

Risk accepted: production engineering begins before the personalization layer has been validated with real users. If M6 reveals the personalization thesis fails, more engineering will need revisiting than if a Wizard-of-Oz phase had caught it earlier.

## Milestone Map

| ID | Milestone | Build-order coverage | Exit gate |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| M0 | Wizard-of-Oz validation | none (manual, no code) | Overridden, May 2026 |
| M1 | Deterministic platform core | #1 session models, #2 knowledge graph, #3 routing, harness scaffold | KG unit tests pass; routing swaps with zero code change; `alembic upgrade head` clean; arc-testable harness skeleton runs |
| M2 | Arc engine + Nightcap arc + safety | #4 arc execution, #5 safety, #7 character behavior | Nightcap arc runs all 3 beats in harness; killer assigned; reveal fires; AI dialogue never leaks knowledge state; L1 hard stops + L2 classification fire pre-generation |
| M3 | Events, API, persistence, telemetry | #6 events, #8 API + auth, #9 persistence, #10 telemetry, #11 full harness | Full session runs through API; events routed by target audience with no leakage; interrupt/resume restores to nearest beat; 5 telemetry signals logging; batch harness runs 10 headless sessions |
| M4 | Nightcap experience layer | none (experience layer, PRD-required) | Real humans play end-to-end on real devices; join under 30s; private info never on shared display |
| M5 | Hardening + proof prerequisites | none (PRD MVP done-criteria) | Adversarial safety playtest complete and blocking issues resolved; per-session gross margin known at each player count; second arc schema designed; Visual Storyworld Phase 1 inspection surfaces live |
| M6 | First qualifying sessions | none (the actual H1 proof) | 5+ completed sessions with outside groups; replay enthusiasm; personalization perception in 2+; run at 4-6 players |

## Sequencing Note

Architecture S15.9 lists the simulation harness as component #11, but the arc execution engine acceptance criteria require a harness. The roadmap therefore splits the harness:

- a minimal arc-runnable skeleton lands at the end of M1
- the full batch and deterministic harness lands in M3

## Operational Companions

- [operations/github-project-setup.md](./operations/github-project-setup.md)
- [operations/working-model.md](./operations/working-model.md)

---

## SOURCE FILE: docs/roadmap/README.md

# Build Roadmap

This directory is the canonical home for Arcwright's execution roadmap.

## Why This Structure Exists

The original roadmap was written as one long planning document. That is useful for human review, but inefficient for AI agents that are usually handed one task, one epic, or one milestone at a time.

This split structure keeps Markdown as the human-editable source of truth while making milestones, epics, and task specs directly addressable.

## Canonical Rules

- Markdown files in this directory are the canonical roadmap source of truth.
- `index.json` is a lookup manifest for agents and scripts. It should match the Markdown files, but it is not authoritative over them.
- If a split file and the architecture or PRD disagree, the architecture or PRD wins. Update the roadmap file.

## GitHub Relationship

- The roadmap in `docs/roadmap/` is the canonical planning source.
- GitHub milestones, issues, and the live project are the execution mirror for work in flight.
- Stable roadmap IDs such as `M1`, `M1-A`, and `AW-101` are the join key between docs and GitHub.
- Live GitHub numbers and URLs should live in `index.json`, not be repeated throughout every Markdown task file.
- If a GitHub issue title and a roadmap ID ever diverge, fix the GitHub title to include the roadmap ID rather than inventing a second identifier.

## Recommended Reading Order

For a human orienting to the build:

1. [00-overview.md](./00-overview.md)
2. The relevant milestone file under [milestones/](./milestones/)
3. The relevant epic file under [epics/](./epics/)
4. The specific task file under [tasks/](./tasks/)

For an AI agent handed a task ID:

1. Open [index.json](./index.json) and locate the task by `id`
2. Read the task file path listed there
3. Read the parent epic and milestone if the task depends on broader context
4. Read the referenced architecture and PRD sections from `docs/architecture/` and `docs/prd/`

For an AI agent handed a GitHub issue number or URL:

1. Read the issue title and extract the roadmap ID such as `AW-101` or `M1-A`
2. Open [index.json](./index.json) and locate that roadmap ID
3. Use the manifest path to open the canonical roadmap file
4. Treat the GitHub issue as execution status and discussion, not the source of truth for scope

## Directory Layout

- `00-overview.md`: roadmap-wide usage, milestone map, decomposition policy, and override notes
- `milestones/`: one file per milestone
- `epics/`: one file per epic
- `tasks/`: one file per agent-sized task spec
- `operations/`: supporting operational docs, such as GitHub project setup and roadmap maintenance notes
- `index.json`: machine-readable manifest for lookup by ID, dependency, and file path

## Maintenance Guidance

- When a future roadmap revision adds or changes tasks, update the split Markdown files first.
- After the Markdown updates, update `index.json` so agents can still locate the right file quickly.
- When a live GitHub issue or milestone is created for a roadmap item, add the cross-reference in `index.json` rather than editing every Markdown file.
- M2 through M6 are decomposed into agent-sized task files as of AW-201. M4 implementation tasks follow the AW-202 Nightcap web experience runtime contract.

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Service architecture library plus thin API monolit 35ab7de354a8812894a3f66681ca4853.md

# Service architecture: library plus thin API monolith at MVP

Date: May 7, 2026
Rationale: Engine is a standalone Python library. API server is a thin HTTP wrapper. Same single deployed process, but engine has zero dependency on web framework. Enforces platform-clean discipline at type system level rather than relying on developer discipline. Alternatives: pure monolith (HTTP context leaks into engine), microservices (overkill for solo founder MVP).
Section: Cross-cutting
Status: Committed

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Session duration is emergent (30-75 min target ran 361b7de354a8815ea6a8c4d4fd6e0951.md

# Session duration is emergent (30-75 min target range). No separate speed round mode.

Date: May 15, 2026
Rationale: Speed round is a fast group plus responsive pacing engine, not a designed configuration. Duration range replaces any session_mode parameter. The pacing engine manages within the 30-75 minute range based on player behavior. Both ends of the range are valid session outcomes.
Section: Cross-cutting
Status: Committed

---
## SOURCE FILE: docs/Session interruption handling partial persistence  358b7de354a881918b78e32f42a98dbd.md

# Session interruption handling: partial persistence (character and knowledge state saved, arc restarts from nearest designed beat)

Date: May 5, 2026
Rationale: On interruption, platform saves character state and knowledge state. On resume, arc restarts from the nearest designed beat. Sessions never restart from the beginning; no state is permanently lost. Full mid-scene resume is deferred as scope debt; beat-level resume covers the most common interruption scenarios and is sufficient for MVP.
Section: Section 2: Strategic Pillars
Status: Committed
Tags: pillars

---
## SOURCE FILE: docs/Session telemetry is a named MVP done-criterion; m 358b7de354a881cfb72cf4a3089bcc7c.md

# Session telemetry is a named MVP done-criterion; must be live from the first production session

Date: May 5, 2026
Rationale: Sessions without structured telemetry are compute cost with no data return. The Tier 2 fine-tuning transition is impossible without accumulated labeled session data. Minimum signals from first production session: arc beat engagement duration, pacing intervention triggers and outcomes, knowledge state constraint activations, session completion status, replay intent indicators. Richer schema designed in Chat 6.
Section: Section 2: Strategic Pillars
Status: Committed
Tags: pillars, roadmap

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Simulation harness full harness for MVP 35ab7de354a881609095c0f142c644b3.md

# Simulation harness: full harness for MVP

Date: May 7, 2026
Rationale: AI-driven synthetic players (Llama 3 on Groq, near-free), seeded deterministic runs, scenario scripting for edge cases, batch run statistics, replay against changed engine versions. 1-2 weeks build. Force multiplier for solo founder iteration: synthetic sessions in minutes vs real playtests in hours. Without it, part-time build pace cannot ship Nightcap. Catches obvious failures but does not predict whether real groups enjoy a session. Real playtests still happen.
Section: Cross-cutting
Status: Committed

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Six behavior commitments for AI characters (stocha 35ab7de354a88194bfcbd46898cb1d74.md

# Six behavior commitments for AI characters (stochastic generation, initiative, NPC-NPC, goal pursuit, per-character profile, arc-level variability)

Date: May 7, 2026
Rationale: (1) Behavior is generated not scripted (non-zero temperature, character voice). (2) Initiative scheduler: AI characters act unprompted based on goals and state. (3) NPC-to-NPC interactions are first-class. (4) Goal pursuit drives behavior, not just colors it. (5) Per-character behavior_profile JSONB column captures initiative threshold, goal pursuit weight, interaction style, variability. (6) Arc-level variability through non-deterministic decision points. These prevent over-predictability and support 'you had to be there' north star.
Section: Cross-cutting
Status: Committed

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Stack positioning Arcwright is narrative runtime m 35ab7de354a88173bc00fc85ed1aab61.md

# Stack positioning: Arcwright is narrative runtime middleware (Layer 2 in game dev stack)

Date: May 7, 2026
Rationale: Arcwright sits between game engines (Unity, Unreal, Godot, web) and AI providers (Anthropic, OpenAI, Groq). Engine handles rendering, input, audio. Arcwright handles arc orchestration, characters, knowledge state, content events. AI providers handle generation. Engine-agnostic and provider-agnostic. Closest analogue: http://Charisma.ai (more controllable, character-level vs session-level). Differentiated from: Convai (3D-native lock-in), Inworld (pivoted), Latitude/Voyage (consumer not platform), Ink/Articy (authored not generative).
Section: Cross-cutting
Status: Committed

---
## SOURCE FILE: docs/Story structure templates as first-class platform  360b7de354a881569cebcc3a3c057045.md

# Story structure templates as first-class platform objects: the current arc schema includes arc_structure as a metadata string field but the engine does not use it to scaffold beat definitions or pacing defaults. Should story structure templates (Dan Harmon, Hero's Journey, etc.) be first-class platform objects that pre-populate beat scaffolding for arc authors, or is this purely an authoring-layer concern deferred to the no-code arc builder in Horizon 2? Resolution must clarify whether arc_structure remains decorative metadata at MVP or whether the engine needs to understand it functionally.

Category: Product
Date Opened: May 14, 2026
Date Resolved: May 15, 2026
Priority: High
Resolution Notes: Resolved in Chat 7 Story Bible. Story Circle is now a first-class platform object. arc_structure: "story_circle" scaffolds 8 pre-populated beat containers with story_circle_step, structural_function, dramatic_purpose, emotional_target, information_goal, tension_target, and character_emphasis fields. The engine uses structural intent as a functional input for generation context, pacing calibration, and ensemble coordination. arc_structure is no longer decorative metadata. arc_structure value changed from dan_harmon to story_circle. Technical Architecture updated to v1.2 with full schema changes. Story structure templates are first-class platform objects at MVP, not deferred to Horizon 2.
Status: Resolved
Where Resolved: Chat 7 Story Bible | 07-Technical-Architecture-v1.2 | 02-Decisions-Log

## SOURCE FILE: docs/The Arcwright platform moat is personalization dep 356b7de354a881fe9704eadcf82b52c3.md

# The Arcwright platform moat is personalization depth, not authoring tooling

Date: May 4, 2026
Rationale: Authoring tooling can be commoditized. The depth of runtime personalization (how well the platform understands who is in the room, their history, preferences, and relationships) is the differentiator that determines the ceiling of what any designed arc can produce. This is an architectural priority, not a product features priority.
Section: Section 2: Strategic Pillars
Status: Committed

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Unified character model with split behavior source 358b7de354a88152813ec5029951f6ed.md

# Unified character model with split behavior source

Date: May 5, 2026
Rationale: Every character (human-controlled or AI-driven) is the same object type: identity, personality profile, goals, knowledge state, relationship graph. Behavior source differs: AI characters have a generation engine; human characters have an input channel. Required for the monster RPG (player and NPC are interchangeable) and for Nightcap (players are characters in the story, not observers).

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Visual scripting committed for H2 H3, schema desig 35ab7de354a88184bf0cf769c4d5bdba.md

# Visual scripting committed for H2/H3, schema designed for visual-builder-readiness now

Date: May 7, 2026
Rationale: Visual scripting (Blueprints model) is a Tier 1 differentiator for designer/storyteller adoption. Authoring at MVP is YAML/TOML files plus Python extension hooks. Visual builder UI is H2 or H3 priority work, built on top of the same schema. Schema is source of truth, visual editor is one possible UI.

## SOURCE FILE: docs/What is the three-layer memory architecture for Ar 363b7de354a881b79638e73e4eb88982.md

# What is the three-layer memory architecture for Arcwright NPCs?

Category: Product
Date Opened: May 17, 2026
Priority: High
Status: Open

Emergence World separates agent memory into three layers: soul entries (identity, never overwritten), episodic memory (what happened, progressively summarized), and world state (established facts). Arcwright needs an analogous design to prevent NPC character drift across long sessions as the context window fills. Without a stable identity anchor layer, NPCs will gradually lose character consistency. This must be decided and designed before engine coding begins. Key questions: what lives in each layer, what gets summarized vs. kept verbatim, and how is the soul layer protected from overwrite.

---

## SOURCE FILE: docs/Which foundation model produces the best NPC chara 363b7de354a881eaad65c16d4c680396.md

# Which foundation model produces the best NPC character consistency for Nightcap's use case?

Category: Product
Date Opened: May 17, 2026
Priority: High
Status: Open

Emergence World's Season 1 ran identical environments with Claude Sonnet 4.6, Gemini 3 Flash, Grok 4.1 Fast, and GPT-5 Mini and found dramatically different behavioral outcomes across worlds. Model choice is therefore a narrative design decision, not just a cost or performance tradeoff. The same character with the same prompt may behave very differently depending on which model powers it. Arcwright should run a comparative test once one NPC is working in Nightcap: same mystery, same NPC profiles, different models, observe behavioral consistency and character fidelity. Must be resolved before committing the engine architecture to a primary provider.

---
